undine

 I. 
 a queer LITTLE child 

 KAROO 
 , red sand , great mound of round iron stone , and bush never very beautiful to look at and now almost burn into the ground by the blaze summer 's sun . an old dutch farmhouse build of the bright red brick to match the ground and stone ; an old stone wall break down here and there at irregular interval , as if to allow for the ready ingress and egress of the hundred enterprising goat , whose delight it be daily to regale themselves on the deformed peach tree and leafless cabbage stalk which the enclosure contain ; an old tent - waggon , whose tent and floor have long go the way of all flesh wood flesh into the fire ; an ancient willow tree , which stand vainly try to reflect itself in a small pond of thick red fluid , and under which may at all time be see a couple of dirty and benighted duck , who there disport themselves under the happy delusion of its being water . 


 all these part compose a picture in which , when look at by daylight , it be hard work to find the slight trace of beauty ; but tonight , penetrate in 

 every nook and corner by the cold white light of an almost full moon , there be a strange weird beauty , a beauty which the veri sheep - soule boer that ever smoke pipe or wear vel - skoen , might feel if he have but one ray of light leave in he . 

 it be a silent night . even the great dog have creep to sleep under the old tent - waggon , and nothing live or move be to be see except a small child and a small ape who be perch in one of the gap of the stone wall . 
 there they have sit for the last hour , never move but very busy cogitate , if one might judge from the grave expression of both face . likely the small ponder on the dire injustice of tie he up all day and give he orange peel in place of orange pulp , and uncracked almond , which all the world know he could not break . his thought might have be the most profoundly philosophical , however , if judge by the appearance of his small black countenance abstruse inquiry into the nature , origin , and destiny of the moon , whose course he be follow with eye hardly less grave and earnest than the large brown pair above he . 

 he be wrap up in the end of the small blue pinafore which the child have on , the only part visible be the small wizard - like face and a small black hand , with which he hold his chin and every now and then raise for a soft sympathetic pat of the little white hand that serve as chin - rest 

 to the white , dark - eyed face above he . the child might have be ten year old , but she look much less as she sit there , perch on the top of a large round stone with her thin little leg draw up under she in a queer little fashion of her own . 

 " Socrates , " she say , presently . the monkey turn his soft brown eye and fix they full on her . 
 " I wish we know , " say the child . 
 Socrates give a long sigh in answer and turn the gaze of his great sad eye back to the slowly move moon .

 the house , as we have say , be Dutch , build in the true dutch style , with one large front room , from which open six or eight cabin - like apartment to serve as bedroom ; and with that indispensable of all dutch farmhouse overhead a great loft . 

 in the front room be two large glass cupboard let into the wall , which in the day of their old dutch proprietor have be will not to contain doll , earthenware , and all the wealth and glory of the household , and which even now , in spite of their 

 be fill with book , have an uncomfortably dutch appearance . the room be well furnish , and light by a great lamp stand on the centre - table . before it , with an open Bible and Prayer Book , sit the farmer : an English Africander with nothing worthy of remark about he , if it be not the unusually fine development of his tall muscular figure and the unusually large amount of yellow hair upon his face . there be five other in the room his wife , a delicate , refined , fair little woman who recline on the sofa his son , handsome and bright - eye , and now home for the holiday and two little dutch girl , grey - eye , yellow - haired , pudding - face , who be here to share with his step - daughter the instruction of the very stiff and upright individual who sit on a chair near the door . this individual wear three curl on each side of her head and carry a large wart on the tip of her chin . 

 " late for prayer again , Undine , " she say , as the owner of the little blue pinafore slip in at the door and take her way to the near seat . 
 no one else take any notice of her entrance , and the chapter be finish they kneel down to pray . Undine do not listen to the prayer but to the great red clock overhead , that be tick away such solemn word , the child think , as she bend below it : 

 " another week go , another day go . what 

 have you do ? we never come back , we moment ; we fly , but we never return , never , never , tick , tick . what have you do with we ? if you do the good you can with all the rest of we , you can never bring one of we back , never , never , tick , tick . " 

 Undine try to listen to the prayer , but the old clock 's voice be loud . 
 " tick , tick , " cry the inexorable old clock , " what good have you ever do ? how be you well able to die now than you be last week ? you be nearer death , but be you ready , ready , ready , tick , tick , tick ? " 
 Undine try to listen to the prayer again , and she catch these word : " thousand , o Lord , be go to destruction every moment . " 
 " yes , yes , yes , " say the clock , " tick , tick , hell , hell , go , go , go , thousand , thousand , thousand , tick , tick , tick , tick . " 

 she could kneel there while the old clock tell only of her own sin and fate , but now when every tick talk of half the world , for whom there be no help , no hope , who be go , go , go she feel as though she be be suffocate and the wall and roof be throb and come down on she . she leap up from her knee , and be recall to a sense of thing present only by be very sharply pull onto they again . fortunately the prayer be almost end , and when they rise there be at once so many human voice try to

 here 
 . your mamma think so . do you not ? " 

 the lady thus appeal to not only fully endorse the opinion , but also , on hear the nature of the offence , ordain that henceforth the offender 's seat should be in the centre of the room , beside her stepfather , and so to speak under the eye of the assembly . this be intend as a direful chastisement , but the child 's thought be still occupy with the ominous ticking of the old clock , and she would have care nothing just then if they have sentence she to sit next some savage king of Timbuctoo who make his meal off little girl . she stand there before they , with the end of the blue pinafore twisted round one small arm which the other be nurse and pat as tenderly as if it have be Socrates .

 " dear God ! great God ! " cry the little child , cover her face with both hand , " you who be so very happy and great and strong , who can do all thing , o dear God ! save they . they be go , go , forever , forever , o God ! God ! " 
 she lie still for some minute and then burst forth again , this time in a perfect agony : 
 " o god ! great God ! save just one soul tonight because I pray . I know that I be wicked and will never be save , but I pray with faith ; save , oh save one soul , for my prayer . great God ! God ! God ! " 

 she sit up and bury her face in both her tremble hand . what be the use of she pray she who do not love God , who could not believe , who could never be save ? how easy it be to understand how the great Son of God could come down to die for soul . the child feel that night as though she , too , could have die to save only a few , a few

 after a time she lie down and try to close her eye and drop asleep ; but now it seem as if already she have pass into that unknown land , prepare by God for the soul at whom he laugh . in Dante 's hell there be fire and fellowship , earth and pain , but in hers there be nothing so merciful or so material . she seem in a wide void in which there be only endless space and blackness , and she have not even two hand , the one of which might touch the other and in touch find fellowship ; and when she cry aloud her voice fall dead upon the air . there be only emptiness , and black space , above , around , below , and she be one alone . oh , how the silence ache ! one throb of pain , one touch , one sound , how blessed they would be . 

 an indescribable terror seize the child . such must be death , eternal death , the death of the wicked , changeless and everlasting as the throne of the God who make it . she creep out of bed

 bling and lie down on the cold mud floor ; that at least be hard and solid , and it seem to calm she . she press her face onto it , and a few burn tear fall on it ; then she lie as still as though she be asleep . how comfort it be , that solid earth ; but it be dead and cold , and she would like the touch of something warm ; so after a time she get up and , noiselessly open the door , stand in the large front room . it be dark and quite still but for the ticking of the old clock and the sound of her own breath . she stand for a minute listening ; then she creep on till her finger touch a door at the far end of the room . after a little pressure it open , and she go in . there be two bed in the room , both occupy , and she kneel down at the foot of the near and stretch out her hand . it come in contact with what she be in search of a small foot , soft and warm and full of life . she hold it for some moment in both hand , and then , afraid of wake the sleeper , rise to go , noiselessly and softly as she have come .

"

" sometimes I feel quite good , and I be sit and read , and I come to something that be quite different from what it be somewhere else . then the devil make I think , how can two thing that say the opposite both be true ? and then I feel wicked and I can not   go on read any more . sometimes , too , when I be pray and I feel as though I love God very much , I remember all at once how it say in the Bible that he never forgive anyone for nothing , but always make some one suffer pain first ; and I remember all the other cruel thing it tell about he ; and then I hate he , and for a long time I can not   pray again . 

 oh dear ! " she say after a little pause . " I wish the world belong to I . I would make it much well ; I would let all the devil out of hell and love they and make they good , so there would be no one to tempt the people any more . do you ever feel so wicked as I do when you be little like I ? " ask Undine , look earnestly at he , as though with the vague hope that his answer might be in the affirmative . 

 " no , I should rather think not , " be the answer . " I use to make little clay oxen and train kid in an old box and enjoy myself ; that be what I use to do when I be your age . " 
 Undine heave a little weary sigh and look at the duck . " I wonder if there be any people in the world who feel like I do and who have such wicked thought , " she say at last . 
 " of course there be , and much wickeder , too ; there be people who do not   believe the Bible be true , or anything else , and they write book also . " 
 " do they ? " say Undine . " I wish I could read they . have you ever ? " 
 " no , " say Frank ; " it be too much bother ; but I will , when I be a man ; " and pull his hat low over his eye , he either make believe to do so or really go to sleep . 

 Undine do not go away , but sit at his foot , nursing Socrates and watch the duck , till the koppie 

 begin to cast long shadow and the fast cool air tell that sunset be not far off . 

 by and by the back door of the house open and the whole family appear equip for their Sunday evening walk all , with the exception of the small dutch girl , who , complain of a headache , be leave to keep Undine company . 
 " take care of everything ; get into no mischief ; and above all remember that it be Sunday , " be the parting injunction which they receive as the group , which now include Frank , move off . 
 the two child stand still watch they till they pass out of sight . then Undine , after cry and pray half the night , and read Edwards and meditate half the day , begin to discover that , she be neither anchorite nor saint , but only a very young animal with much wild blood in its young vein that need circulate . it may have be the evening 's cool that make she conscious of this , for it seem to have an inebriate effect upon Socrates , who leap , grin , and turn somerset in a manner truly astonishing . 

 " I wonder , " say Undine , " if Socrates and I be to run a race , which of we would beat " ; and without wait for a reply , she set about test the matter at once . with one end of his chain hold firmly in her hand they set off , but have not go thirty pace when it have slip out and Socrates , chain and all , be make his way to the near koppie , with 

 jingling , screeching and leaping , much to the mingled horror and delight of his little pursuer . the delight soon vanish , however , for , the koppie reach , Mr. Socrates feel himself quite in his own element , and absolutely refuse to be cozen by soft word or specious promise . seat himself on the top of a large round stone , he would very leisurely stretch out his leg , scratch himself , and then look up into the blue sky with an air of melancholy abstraction ; this till his breathless pursuer be within half a foot of he ; then , with a whirl , a cry , and a somerset , off to another and more inaccessible stone , round which his little pursuer might dance and beseech in vain , leap to catch the tip of the chain he leave hang almost within reach of her finger . it be uncertain how long this game might have continue have not the idea enter Socrates ' small head that more fun might be get from scamper over the roof at home than by remain where he be . 


 accordingly , he be off like an arrow , while Undine follow he breathlessly , minus one shoe and with more rent in her garment than could well be count . arrive at the house , she find the exemplary Sennie stand exactly where and as she have leave she ; except that she have place one finger in her mouth and partly turn her head to look at Socrates , who be now on the roof of the house , 

 busily occupy in pull out thatch and work away with the great dispatch and precision . 

 Undine quickly see that , if this be allow to go on for many minute , he would have work his way into the loft and perhaps to a bloody death as the reward of his evil deed . 
 what be to be do ? she look at the little dutch girl in despair ; the little dutch girl look at she . 
 " he be naughty , " say that little maiden at length , and then slowly replace the finger she have take out of her small mouth . Undine turn away in disgust ; there be no help to be get from she , and nothing for it but to climb the roof herself and capture he . 
 with much difficulty a long ladder be bring which reach just to the top of the wall ; and this be soon mount . once there , how to get on to the ridge be the question ; for at every touch the old thatch crumble away by handful , and she have not crawl many inch before it seem inevitable that she should soon find herself deposit among the skin in the loft or with the thatch upon the ground . 

 " you will fall down and die , " say the little dutch girl , very deliberately , as she watch Undine 's perilous ascent with almost as much interest as Socrates , who have now take his seat on one of 

 the gable , and with his chin rest on his hand be contemplate her movement most attentively . 

 Undine take no notice of either , but continue to climb , do more harm at every move than Socrates in twenty . the ridge be gain at last , after infinite trouble , but not so Socrates . he wait till her finger touch his tail ; and then , with that appendage cock high in air , walk off very quietly to the other gable , where he ensconce himself far more comfortably than his little pursuer find it possible to do at her . there be no get down again , for the first step down would have be on the ground ; there be nothing to be do but sit still and wait . consequently the appalling and shocking spectacle which meet the eye of the upper power , on their return home , be Undine , shoeless , kappieless and tear , seat on the ridge and hold on with one arm to the gable , while at the other end Socrates , with clank chain and tail in air , be dance a true devil 's quadrille . never be worthy parent and instructor , on their return from a quiet Sabbath ramble , meet by so horrific and wrath - rouse a sight . 
 a second ladder be quickly get and undine safety deposit upon the ground , where she be instantly march off into the house to answer for her evil conduct . 
 " how do you get into this plight , you wicked , wicked little girl ? " say her mother . 

 Undine stand with her hand cross and her eye fix on the one little white toe that have force its way out of the stocking . 
 " I do not mean to , " she say , feel very contrite and not a little ashamed of herself . 
 " do not mean to ! of course not ! you never mean to do anything that you do . the wind loosen Socrates and blow you both up onto the roof of the house ! of course it do ; we all know that it do . " 
 Undine feel very much inclined to say that she be sorry and be not go to do so any more ; then she remember that say so might make her punishment less , so she stand still and look down at her toe . 
 the lean and lanky individual now strike in her note . 
 " Undine , my dear Undine , " she say in a very low and subdued voice , " if you continue this course of action , what will become of your immortal soul ? what will become of it ? " 
 this be too much for Undine who have stand still to receive her bullying , fill with contrition and repentance ; it raise all the evil in her nature . " I know I be wicked and I do not   care , and I do not   care what become of my soul , and I be not afraid of anything , " say Undine , lift up her face and throw back her long tangle hair defiantly . 

 " be there ever in this world so evil dispose 

 and ungodly a child ? " say her spiritual guide , shake her head solemnly . " go to bed , undine ; go to bed ; I shall say no more to you . " 

 " good - night , " say Undine and she walk off to her room with almost a smile upon her face . but once there and alone , she fling her tired little body across the foot of the bed and cry bitterly . 
 " oh , I wish I be dead ! I wish I be dead ! there be nobody like I , and nobody love I . oh , I wish I be dead ! " and at last , without undressing , fall asleep .

 III . 
 the MAN with the mouth 

 as aunt MARGARET

 IV . 
 go to CHAPEL 

 EVERY

 V. 
 a sunny afternoon and a WILD night 

 IT be

 her grandmother meet she at the door , cry and wring her poor weak hand : " oh , he be dead ! Poor Frank be dead ! they have find his body , and the boy 's that be with he . and my darling , my poor darling , where be she ? it will kill she ! it will kill she ! " 
 Undine do not stay to mingle tear with she , but pass from room to room like one in a dream , search where yet she do not hope to find ; with the restless move water ever before her eye as she wearily close and open door after door . 

 the door of her own room stand half open , but she only glance in , and be just leave it when her ear catch a sound from the corner near the window . there , with the sunlight stream full over its yellow hair , crouch a naked human figure . the knee be draw up till the chin rest on they , and one arm be clasp tight round they ; the other be stretch out , and one finger point to a crack in the board . the eyebrow be draw down till the eye be hardly visible , but they open slightly every time the mouth twitch nervously to one side or the other . 
 Undine stand motionless in the doorway and watch it . have sorrow touch her reason ? be she mad ? or be that really what she look for that thing with the fade yellow flower in its hair ? 
 " ha - ha - ha ! " 
 ' twas a hellish laugh that fill the room and ring out across the rose tree in the garden . the finger be still point to the crack along the board . 

 " ha - ha - ha ! there they come one , two , three ; there they come the devil that have get his soul , hundred of they , thousand of they . that be the door they take he down , there . I ask God to take I instead , but he would not , and now they have get I too . he use to say there be no God , and no hell , but God will show he now . 

 ha - ha - ha ! how they come ! little devil one , two , three ! " 

 Undine utter a low cry and drop down onto her knee beside she . 
 the yellow thing , with its fade flower , crouch down lower , crouch till its chin rest on the floor , and its half - close eye glance furtively now on this side now on that . then spring to its foot , with a cry , it seize Undine with both hand and bear she to the ground . kneel on she and put its lip close to her ear , it hiss forth : " I know you , who you be . you look like Undine ; but you be the devil ; the devil to whom God give his soul . I know , I know . you leave his body lie there upon the beach , and you tore it with your cruel hand that I might not know it when I find it lie there in the grey dawn : but I know it , I know it . " she fix her tooth in Undine 's arm and clasp she to her breast until Undine 's cry be smother and she become unconscious . when those who have hear they enter the room , Undine lie upon the floor insensible , and in the far corner crouch a thing that lick its red lip and cry exultingly as it point at she : " I have kill the devil ! I have kill the devil ! ha - ha - ha ! " 
 a week after , and Cousin Barnacles have take Undine to his house in Greenwood . 

 it be not time which make old man and woman of we . Undine 's childhood lie bury in the grave 

 upon the hillside where a form which the sea have give up be lay , and in a dark strong house far off where a mad woman grow wilder still if they show she a bible or a yellow flower . 

 Ignorant of the world , shy , childish in her manner , yet for her childhood be forever of the past . she would never again dance with naked foot among the rock and wonder how , in the world of green and gold , man ever sigh and pray for rest beneath its crust . for she , henceforth , the merry laugh child would be you , and grave - eyed man and woman , we and we . 



 VI . 
 GREENWOOD 

 IT be 
 a white lifeless face that Cousin Jonathan bring with he to Greenwood . so ghastly and pale that even Mrs. Goodman and Miss Mell , if they be not move to pity , could not find it in their heart to exercise their tongue upon it . 

 all day Undine use to wander in the old wood that lie between Cousin Jonathan 's house and the village ; use to wander there when the dry leaf be fall down in shower and pile themselves up in little grave - like heap at the root of the great tree ; use to look at they and fancy , with a kind of apathetic pleasure , that , when the spring come with its young green , she , like the leaf , would have vanish away . she think her heart be break . perhaps it be ; but she do not know that heart be only Time 's china cups china cup which the old father be forever throw hither and thither , crack and smash in his wild reckless way , and then carefully pick up and cement so cleverly that the old scar do not even show . they may ring a little dead if you strike they but that be all . 

 not know this , Undine wonder at herself when she find out that she intend to live , and to grow strong , and pretty too . 
 then the woman in the village begin to say malicious thing , and to find out that she be stupid and conceited and unchildlike ; but she care nothing for what they say , and read her book and curl herself up to dream for hour among the root of her favorite old tree by the little bridge in the wood . at first they be sad , unearthly dream , but when the year grow old and the golden colour come creep over the hill , it creep into her dream also ; and she would sit there smile and glad ; then she would wonder at herself and go home slowly , think of the dark lonely house and the Goldenlight that be bury there forever . 
 Cousin Jonathan try to cheer she , buy book for she , a horse , dress and trinket , and everything wherewith man seek to comfort and delight the heart of womankind . but , as his wife remark to Miss Mell , he might as well have save his money and spar himself the trouble : she never show the least pleasure at receive his prettiest gift , except it happen to be a book that please she , and then it be only in a staid , old - womanish way . 

 three year have pass by , and Undine the child have change into Undine the woman pretty , very pretty , even Miss Mell be oblige to allow that , " for those who like that style of beauty . " but she

People leave off have anything to do with she at last . 

 " I be terribly anxious about she , " Mrs. Barnacles would say . " it be not that she be old ; she be a mere child ; but I do not   see what be to make her change ; and if no one ever see she , who be to marry she ? " Mrs. Barnacles be a yellow - face big - nosed invalid , who pass her life on a sofa and be apt to take a dyspeptic view of thing . " she have need of all her good look , if she be to go off ; man do not   take readily to those queer , dull sort of girl ; and with those idiotic idea of her , on religious matter , too , half the man would not have she as a gift . " 
 " of course they would not , " Miss Mell would here strike in ; " and I believe it be all put on too she not go to chapel and all the rest of it just to be peculiar . it be all nonsense . what do she know about such thing ? for clever learn man it be all very well , but a stupid child like she ought to be well whip and feed on bread and water for six month ; that would take the nonsense out of she well than anything else . " 

 " yes , " Mrs. Barnacles would assent , " for man it be all very well , as you say ; but a woman , and one who live on charity , ought to keep they to herself if she have idea of that unwomanly kind . " 
 she use to tell Undine all this , to her face , sometimes : " go to chapel and give up read those nonsensical book , and act like other people even if you do not   think like they . it will not   answer , it will not   answer at all ; and you have well give up all this sort of thing before it be too late . you will repent it if you do not . " 
 then Undine , half bitter , half indifferent , would get away from she to the dear old world of inanimate nature , which never call we queer and strange or advise we to wear a mask . it be well for she that she care for that at least , for dark loveless time have fall on she , and she care for nothing else . Cousin Jonathan be good to she , do all in his power for she , but she like he less as the year go on . she have never love he , and the intellectual help which he have be able to give she cease to be a bond between they when she have reach his ground and even pass beyond he . so now Cousin Jonathan share the fate common to all lover , and give out his gold , such as it be , for dust .

 VIII . 
 BEAUTIFUL SNOW 

 it be 
 a cold wintry afternoon and the white snow cloud be lie low and heavy . undine , after many almost sleepless night , creep down to the little parlour and have a fire make there , the first that have be make since Cousin Jonathan leave . 

 Miss Mell , now her friend be get well , have offer to come and sit up with she ; and Undine , as she nestle down in the great armchair , look forward to a long evening of drowsy rest . Prince lie sleep before she with his head at her foot , and she , half doze , watch the little spark as they flutter up the chimney . so short , so warm , so bright ; how pleasant the life of a spark must be ! 
 " you seem to find something very absorbing in the contemplation of the fire this evening , " say a voice beside she ; and Prince , wide awake in an instant , leap up to greet his master . 
 " you quite startle I , " she say . " I do not think you would come tonight ; it be get almost dark . " 

 " yes ; we have the promise of a heavy fall of 

 snow , " he say , as he seat himself in an armchair on the other side of the fire .

 " no , I never miss he . you have well keep he if he be any pleasure to you , " answer the Piece - of - perfection , stretch out one delicate white hand to the dancing flame . 
 after a short silence he say , " do you never wish to return to Africa ? " 
 " no , " she reply . " I know no one there . my stepfather have remarry . but I should like to see the old farm and my little monkey 's grave again . " 
 he be lean back now with his face in the shadow ; she could not see the line she dread at the corner of his mouth , so she answer , " yes , he be the good friend I have . " 
 another pause follow ; then he say , more abruptly than be his will not , " I have a favour to ask of you , Miss Bock . 

 " you rather puzzle I , " he say . " I never feel sure I understand you , and I do most man . at time I form an opinion of you , at time another , but 

 I never feel sure that I be right . I wish you could satisfy my curiosity and explain to I how it be you come to have such extraordinary view and manner . " 

 " why do you not put some other word in the place of " extraordinaryí say , " pernicious , í " reprehensibleí ? that be what you really think , " she reply , use a free speech with he than ever before , for in the firelight the band of speech be loose and the tongue of man and woman do wonder . 
 he never pay her compliment or speak to she as he would to another woman , so he answer quietly , " those word would be almost too strong ; say , unwomanly . " 
 another make this remark would have be answer by a contemptuous silence ; or at good she would have launch out into a denunciation of that singular injustice which cramp and dwarf a woman 's mind , make it an unpardonable offence against her womanhood to entertain a thought or give utterance to an idea that have not be repeat and režchoed till it be as stale and unpalatable as a last year 's loaf . tonight she only say : " why be they unwomanly ? what be your idea of what a woman ought to be ? " 

 " you be ask I a question hard to answer , " he reply , look with his half - close eye into the fire . " a woman to be womanly should have nothing strike or peculiar about she ; she should 

 shun all extreme in manner and mode of expression ; she should have no strong view on any question , especially when they differ from those of her surrounding ; she should not be too reserved in her manner , and still less too affable and undignified . there be between all extreme a happy mediate , and there a woman should always be find . man may turn to one side or the other ; woman never must . " 

 Undine say nothing when he end . she could not help it ; she have be bear with strong and determined idea on every subject , sub- and superlunar , and not one step of her sixteen year ' journey have she walk in the happy mediate road . it be too late to change now . they have tell she that the day would come when she would repent have do nothing to try to conform herself , at least outwardly , to the view of other ; and she do repent it as she sit there that evening . she would have part with all that be high and good in herself to become a little less Undine , a little more like anyone else . who be this man , what be he , that he should make her grovel so ? she ask herself . 
 " you have not yet answer I , " say the Piece - of - perfection , again stretch out his delicate hand to the blaze . " be you go to satisfy my curiosity ? "

 he 
 ; and she say so . 


 " nothing ! and you have live for sixteen year and in two continent , and certainly be not trouble with lack of idea . you must excuse I , however . I have no right to press you in this way . "

 Albert Blair sit and listen without the shade of a sneer upon his lip . 
 Most man have their moment of insanity , which belie and be at variance with all the day and year of the past and will find no successor in the future , moment when their thought and feeling be oppose to all they have ever deem rational , right or possible . 
 such moment come for the first time and the last to the Piece - of - perfection as he sit listen to Undine in the firelight .

 forget all this , bewitch , befool , infatuate , he stretch out his hand to the little figure opposite he .

 " come to I , darling , " he say , hold out his hand to she . 
 still she sit and look at he ; then he draw she softly to his arm , and she nestle close to he . 
 she do not kiss he or speak : only clung to he and rest with her arm round his neck and her head on his shoulder . 
 if she lay there hour or moment , she do not know ; it be enough to be there .

 what be the past ? what be the future ? the present be enough . she answer , " no . "

 " yes . "

" so he leave she .

 " that I will try and be everything you wish . do you believe I ? "

 she throw herself down among the pillow , and after half an hour rise slowly to begin her packing . when it be do she go to Mrs. Barnacles ' room , to tell she that she be leave that evening .

 X. 
 melt SNOW 

 how 
 white , how white and dazzling , that road upon the hillside lay ! 

 all day she sit at the window , watch it . in the dusk , when no other eye could mark it , she see it wind in the dimness . all night in her dream it lie before she , in its white ache emptiness . 
 how slowly the chill week crawl over her two , four , six , eight . still she watch it till the colour fade from her cheek and the bright restless light grow strong in her eye . her old grandmother would lay her work aside and , stand behind she , would stroke her hair softly with her old wither hand and say , " you be not well my child ; you be lonely ; the place be too quiet for you ; a young life like yours should not be bury away here . " 
 and Undine would answer nothing , and sit watch , only she know for what . 
 the snow have vanish and the road lay , a white chalky line between the brown field ; only now and then a farmer 's cart or a labourer from the next village would pass along it . 

 " why do you never sit by the fire ? it be so cold and cheerless at the window , and there be nothing to be see , " the old woman would say . but still she sit there , look out and stitch away always at delicate white muslin with pink bow and dreamy blue and white stuff , which the old woman think make she look like an angel when she try they on . 
 " the child have change , " she would say to herself , as she sit knitting and doze in the firelight . " she never read now and think only of dress and music ; but I suppose it be natural ; the young will be young . " 
 the winter go early that year , and the first sign of spring be show themselves . Undine do not count the day any more ; she do not reason or ask herself any question ; she only wait , wait . 
 one day she see a boy come down the road . it be quite midday and the sun be shin with an almost summer - like warmth . she sit there with her hand fold in her lap , look at he yet not see he till he come up to the open window and put a letter in her hand . 
 she start up and pass out through the next room , where her grandmother sit knit in the sunshine of the open door . 
 " what be it ? what have happen ? " ask the old woman ; but Undine only hurry past she with the letter press tight in both hand against her breast . 

 through the long leafless garden she pass , 

 where the soft bud be just begin to swell under the brown bark , through the rough uneven meadow beyond , and sit down at the side of the little cozy river that creep slowly between its muddy reedy bank . she sit long look at the paper in her hand , with its great red seal ; then she tear it open .

 then , a sudden wild impulse seize she . she must rise she must run she must flee she must go somewhere , anywhere .

 stone , climb it , and run on among the tree and rock that lie scatter on its summit . she do not seem able to get far ; again and yet again she think she find herself in the same place ; and every time she look up at the great red sun it seem a great , laughing , cruel human eye , look down at she from the clear blue sky . 

 it be on she , on she , wherever she go , that great blood - red eye , and the great brown hill opposite with its white chalk road be like a leer human face that laugh at she , jeered at she , mock at she ; and the stone , and the tree they have all a hide sneer about they . " Fool ! fool ! fool ! " they cry . and the blue cloudless sky overhead be so hard and pitiless , like a righteous human soul which have no mercy for the erring . " o sky , blue cloudless sky , have pity , have pity on I ! " she cry in her madness ; and she throw herself down and lie on a great flat stone in the footpath . gaze up into the sky 's blue depth , she look straight at the dazzle sun with an unnatural strength of sight . 
 they drive her madder , madder , the sky , the sun , the earth ; till she writhe in her pain , like a trodden worm , on the ground and stone . then the old feeling come over she again , and she rise up and run . her sight seem to grow dim and blur at last , and she stumble and fall again and yet again over the stone and stump . bruise , bleed , she feel nothing , only know she must run on , on . 

 her grandmother look out anxiously for she all day , and when it be grow dark that evening , see she walk slowly up the little garden path , with her head droop on her breast and her arm hang heavily at either side . 
 " where have you be , my child ? " she say , come out to meet she . " be you not bitterly cold ? " 
 " no , " say Undine , wearily ; and when they enter the little parlour with its cheerful lamp and firelight her grandmother notice that the bright anxious light she be accustom to see in her eye have vanish . 
 " you look ill , my child , " she say , rest her nervous old hand softly on her arm . 
 " I be not ill , " Undine say , " only tired . no , I be not hungry ; I only want to rest . I be tired , very tired . I want no light , thank you . good - night . " 



 XI . 
 a clever LITTLE man and a poor little FOOL

 Albert Blair be not a cruel man . a man of high principle , the world say . a man to whom no one in trouble ever appeal in vain for help . a man who never give his horse or dog a blow more than be necessary a good master , a good man , as the world go . yet he feel no sorrow for the young life he have crush . it have to be do , and he do it as he beat his dog or discharge his servant when necessary .

 a VERY wicked woman

 she sit there till the last glow have fade from the hilltop and the grass on which they sit begin to grow damp and cold . 

 " my little friend , I be very cruel to wish to keep you . would life have more of happiness for you than it have have for I ? a little gladness out of colour and light ; a little sweetness out of dream ; one hour of bliss look at footmark in the white snow ? be that enough to make it worth keep ? oh , my little friend , it will be well to go . you 

 have make a little brightness . there be nothing well wait for you if you stay . " 

 " not in bed yet ? " say her husband when , return late the next evening from a dinner he have be attend in the neighbouring town , he find his wife still up and sit on a low chair with the child on her knee . " you might as well have go with I if you mean to sit up so late . you will never get your rose back if you go on in this way . 
 " I can not go to bed tonight , " she say , quietly , smooth softly the crumple in the child 's little nightdress . " it be very ill . " 
 " Ill ? what be the matter ? " he say , peer down into its face for a moment . " it look just as usual to I . I suppose that fool of a doctor have be frightening you . " 
 " no ; he say there be no cause to be anxious just tonight , but I can see more than he can . " 
 " oh , we all know you can see through a wall , but it would be more sensible of you to go to bed and rest , " respond her master , sullenly , as he turn away and leave the room . 
 " would not touch the baby at first , or have it bring near she ; go and make a fool of herself over it now , " he grumble . " could not   see that it be ill , and think it be die now . she be a queer composition . " 

 it be a warm night for that time of year , and 

 Undine have open the great door and window on both side of the room to let in the air . yet the lamp that hang overhead burn steadily and throw down its unwavering steady light over mother and child . on the mantelpiece the bronze clock tick regularly , but the breathing of the child be so low it could not be hear . 

 perhaps she be very foolish , after all ; the doctor must know good ; and she look down inquiringly . there be just the faint smile about the little mouth and the hand be cross loosely on the little breast . as she look the smile pass slowly and the child open wide its eye and fix they on the lamp overhead those large , unearthly deep brown eye . 
 Undine would not move for fear of disturb it , but the baby turn its head round slowly , and look up into her face with those great calm eye . do they speak to she or do she only fancy it ? those dark awful eye of her own little child . there be no dread , there be no questioning in they , but a calm , solemn light . 
 Undine look deep , deep into they . she do not hear the clock strike or know how the moment pass , till the white lid drop slowly . there be no sigh , there be no change , but when she lay her hand upon its breast she know that the baby be dead . 

 she rise up and carry its body to the large white 

 bed , and lay it down just as it be with its peacefully cross hand . then she drop down on her knee beside it with her forehead on the ground , and the dead be not more motionless than the living . 

 the next morning when her husband , have be rouse early and tell of his child 's death , go out in search of Undine , he find she sit in the sunshine on the dewy grass . 
 " it be dead , " she say , look up at he with a calm , cloudless face , as though she have say , " it be asleep . " he wonder , for how should he understand the love she bear her child , the passionless love , love it in spite of its be her ? the baby I love , because it be mine ; the woman I cling to against my reason I must hear they , see they , touch they , or be devour by a senseless gnawing ; but the friend whose soul have reach mine , the thing I have love for what it teach I , I let they pass without a tear , for my part of they remain with I , and for the rest , let it go . 

 " you have hear the news , of course , " say Miss Mell one morning before she have enter Mrs. Barnacles ' room . she be very much out of breath , for she be grow asthmatic of late . " Harry Blair have come . I see he myself half an hour ago , and he say his father be dead . do you ever hear of such a thing ? some people 
 be 
 lucky , " say Miss Mell with energy . 


 " why , I do not   think he will get much . do his father leave he anything ? " 
 " leave he anything ! of course he do not . you may be sure she would take good care of that . I can see it now just as well as if it be past how she will come here lord it over everybody and marry a big swell before the year 's out . with all her money and her bold , free manner , man be sure to be take by she . I be sure she have no good look to talk of , but they be such fool they never see it . they be so easily take in . " 
 " even if they be , I do not   wonder that you never manage to do it , " think Mrs. Barnacles ; but she only reply : " I do not   know anything about she . I have   never hear she mention since her baby die two year ago . I have   never have but two note from she since she leave . Gratitude be and never will be one of Undine Blair 's virtue . " 
 Mrs. Barnacles refrain from make any further animadversion on the character of her connection ; for it strike she that should Miss Mell 's prognostication be verify , it would be just as well to have a smile for the young heiress and get the benefit of some of the fruit and game that would be plentiful at Blair House . indeed , it would be rather pleasant than otherwise to have all Greenwood ride over the head by a connection of her , provide only that she be not include in the everybody . 

 Miss Mell , whose aversion for Undine be of the 

 same nature as that of a cat for water , or a Kaffir for work , quite irrepressible , inherent and inextinguishable , continue to express her opinion of the character of her natural enemy with asperity that might not be rival . she be just remark on the perfidy of her behaviour towards Harry Blair , when Cousin Jonathan 's mild blue eye look in at the door . 

 " do come in , Mr. Barnacles . you have   hear the news , no doubt ; perhaps you have   see Mr. Blair ? " 
 " yes , he call on I as soon as he arrive . he be on the continent when he get the news of his father 's illness , and come to find he dead . " 
 " poor fellow ! do he really expect to get anything ? " say Miss Mell , in a voice expressive of infinite scorn at his credulity . 
 " no ; he be astonish when he get home to find that the property be to be divide equally between the two brother . he have no idea of any such thing . " 
 " so the old man leave she nothing ? " say Miss Mell . 
 " no , " assure Cousin Jonathan ; " he leave she everything , but she be go off , nobody know where , and have leave an order that everything be to be divide between they . Harry Blair have come here to enquire whether I know anything about she . " 

 " I should say the good thing would be to let she alone , " say Miss Mell ; " she have evidently get some nice little game of her own to play . " but Miss Mell 

 be discomfit . Hitherto her abhorrence of that red - cheeked , scheme affectation have be of a groundless kind , accountable only on the hypothesis of natural antipathy . other girl as pretty do not arouse the latent feline propensity of her nature in anything like the same degree ; it would not have give she half the infinite satisfaction to efface 
 their 
 beauty with thumb and finger nail that she would have have in operate on the cheek of the scheming affectation . but now , to be prove a daughter of Belial , a false prophetess , by Undine obstinately refuse to commit the evil prophesy of she : be it not just cause for bitterness ? 

 saint make perfect forgive such injury , but not a wrinkle woman on the rotten side of forty , with no money or intellect to keep the wine of life from turn sour in her bottle . 
 she sit there wish Undine might be go to the devil , as Alice Brown have go in verification of her prophecy of six year before . she do not stay long , however , and find it hard work to change the expression of her countenance to one of serene affability as she pass young Mr. Dunstables in the street . 

 after she have go , Cousin Jonathan sit down to smoke and read a sermon . it be a good cigar , but it have not   any flavour ; it be a nice sermon , original , by Henry Ward Beecher , but he do not   like it . he have not feel so many nasty twinge since he 

 have read a certain marriage notice in the paper year before . " I be grow too studious , " he say ; " my nerve be debilitate , seriously debilitate . I must take a tonic . I must take a walk . " 

 exercise be good for debility of many kind , and he come home feeling well . 
 while he be walk in a desperate hurry with fly arm up the hill , Harry Blair be wander in a desultory manner among the tree below . Cousin Jonathan be more light of heart than he have be for many a brown day : 
 " she be not so evil as they think she , not so mercenary , " he say , and rejoice . 



 XIV . 
 ON BOARD SHIP to south AFRlCA 

 on that 
 Wednesday morning the cause of the violent exercise of the former and the joy of the latter be stand on board a steamer bind for South Africa . 

 Undine be lean over the side of the ship and turn back no wistful look to the fast recede english shore . like a great impassioned living creature whose burn , strive heart impel it to wander on forever , the steamer pass over the blue , breezy , swell sea , leave its track of foaming bubble to dance and die in sunshine . the wild free sea - bird , as they dip their wing into the water and spread they out in the morning light , be glad and full of life . 
 it be such rest to stand and watch they , it be long before she turn her eye to the little world on deck . there be motion enough there also , and happiness too for all that might be see ; but Undine look back longingly at her sea - bird as they float over the water , as though it might be pleasanter to be among they than among the wise fowl that trot on the deck . 

 near she be sit two Africander girl who have be send home for their education , and who be return sublimely ignorant of everything in general and their own deficiency in particular , to make a grand sensation in their little up - country town , to be worship and seek after by the sterner sex and woefully traduce and servilely copy by the gentler , who would for a short time look up to they as Young Lady 's Journals in the flesh and worthy of all imitation from their collar to their walk . 

 far off there be a portly dame wear the stiff of black silk with the stiff of neck , who could by no conceivable effort bring her eye low than the great gold ring that adorn her short finger , and who devoutly believe this ball have be launch into space and continue suspend there to serve as a floor whereon might be place her well - shod foot . long ago she have do her own ironing , and her own washing too at a pinch when no Kaffir maid be to be get , but her husband have be a lucky emigrant and those day be forget now . her husband , who sit not far from she , look as though the rolling of the ship be considerably more than he could stand and fervently wish himself in old Africa again : old Africa , to which he would return small and wise after his travel , the truth have be reveal to he 

 dur- 
 during 


 e his wandering that the world have great thing than a british settler . to his wife no revelation have be make , for the darkness that surround the female soul be dense . 


 a little to the right of this couple be stand a pimply young missionary , bite his nail and star very hard at a very pretty blonde who be go to the Cape to be marry and who fill his bosom with those gentle stirring to which the sacerdotal breast be strangely prone . she look not at he , but from under her black silk hat her dove 's eye glance softly at a group of young Englishmen , bird of a feather , who stand together smoke and chatting . a fish in the hand be worth six at the hook , and more than one bride have come out to her beloved to find herself unwanted ; so , if there be any golden fish on board , it might be as well to angle for they . the young gentleman on whom her eye be rest now be small game , however puny , white - faced young Londoners , " raw Englishmen " they would be call out in the colony , where they would no doubt go into store as clerk or become petty diamond - buyer at the Fields . there be one or two german Jews on deck , smoking cigar and sun themselves , some go out for the first time and some return to the cape : not the little snivel , weasel - like creature who come out third class and , as soon as they land , supply themselves with a waggon and a couple of mule 

 and become " smouse , " 
 1 
 hawk false jewellery and damage clothing among the dutch farmer , and grow rich on it ; but gentlemen Jews , with their polite foreign manner and their fascinating break English , who will make you swear round be square and sell you to the devil before your face , and you shall never know it ; who will squeeze you to pulp to get your last shilling today , and tomorrow , when your wife be starve and no Christian will help she , will give she ten . 

 there be man and woman of all shape and quality to be see , but nothing so pleasing as two little child with pretty face who stand near to she . innocent blue eye and pink - and - white dimpled face be surround by a maze of fine yellow hair . presently a very diminutive and equally ugly terri with a white body and little yellow ear come up , and receive from the foot of the small of the two an astonishingly lusty kick . 
 " oh , Lily , how can you ! " say her sister . " it belong to that lady in the black - silk dress . " 
 " no , it do not , or I would not have kick it , " respond the little one ; " it belong to that woman with the plait hair and the old grey frock . " 
 " oh , then it be all right , " answer the elder , complacently . 

 1 
 " smouse " hawker , peddler . use in English , the word rhyme with " house " ; in Afrikaans it rhyme with the english word " dose . " 


 Undine stoop down to caress the shabby little creature whom the world ill use because its mistress have not a chin or a silk dress . even in a morsel of humanity not three foot high , with a baby face and golden curl , must one find the world , the flesh , and the devil full grow ? 
 she look away from they to the woman with the plait hair and the grey dress . she be shabby , dreadfully shabby . her grey skirt have be turn not only inside out but upside down ; her loose cloth jacket have once be black but be now brown , and , to judge from its cut , be the last relic of a long - deceased fashion . on her head she wear a great round hat ornament round the crown by a piece of brown lace which must have be young when the jacket be black . her black glove be three size too large for she and yet do not conceal the knobby condition of her long thin hand . she have a weak , nervous mouth and sit on the edge of the bench , as though hardly sure she have a right to be there at all . her hand be cross in her lap and her eye look out across the water . Immense wonderful steel - grey eye that be strangely out of keep with the wrinkle wizened face in which they be set . 
 " I wonder who that woman in the grey dress be , " say a gentleman stand in earshot of Undine to his companion , a military man who boast an immense pair of moustache and a most elegant drawl . 

 " woman in grey dress ? I see one just now . deuce pretty little thing . try to get up a conversation ; could not . well - look thing on board . " 
 " then she be not the woman I mean , " respond his companion . " she be not your style , would not exactly attract you , but she have marvellous eye . " 
 " who have ? " inquire the captain 's pretty sister , come up at that moment . possess a pair of eye as remarkable for their brilliancy as the shabby woman 's be for their shadowy deepness , she think the remark refer to none other than herself . 
 " I can not   say that I admire your taste , " she say when the owner of the grey eye have be point out to she . " a living song they be , you say ? you who have so much of the poet 's blood should really try and translate they into something intelligible to we poor mortal who see nothing in she but a piece of very shabby gentility . you poet should not absorb all the light that fall on you without reflect a ray on we . " 

 " I be afraid it take more to make a poet than nature have pour into my mould , " he answer , laugh lightly , as he offer she his arm and walk off with the graceful black - eyed beauty . undine think his dance blue eye as pleasant to look at as the ripple wave , and stand watch as he pass to and fro , now stop to throw bonbon to the child or stoop to stroke the yellow- 

 and - white terri they have kick , then stand to chat with a lady or raise his hat and turn his face against the breeze to let it toss and play with his brown curl . a boy he seem in his perfect enjoyment of life in spite of his rich brown beard , the only glad childish thing on board . Undine 's eye follow he and she forget the shabby woman till she go down to her cabin and find that she be to be her companion there . 

 it be well than have the captain 's pretty sister or any of the gay butterfly on board ; and truly well she find it when , lie down in her berth , she do not rise from it for week . the strain under which she have live for year , the excitement of the last few week , have tell on she , and now when it be all past she break down utterly . after a few day she be well enough to lie still and enjoy the quiet rest , but be weak enough to feel grateful for the silent constant attention of her companion , who sit beside her night and day . 
 " you be very good to I , very good , " say Undine one day , when the woman sit bath her head with vinegar and water . " you do everything for I so much well than the stewardess can . " 
 " I ought to be able to , " say the woman in a low , nervous voice . " I have be nurse for twelve year . I do nothing else . " 

 all day Undine 's occupation be to lie and watch she , for she never go on deck but sit there 

 sew- 
 sewing 


 ing at innumerable little white shirt and petticoat , with those great marvellous grey eye which always seem look beyond the object on which they be fix to something far away . 

 she might have be any age between twenty and forty , for in spite of the wrinkle in her sallow face there be something more of the girl than the woman about she . 
 she never speak unless speak to , till one day Undine have scribble half a dozen line of rhyme in which she tell what she feel when there have be rain in the night and she go out to see the rose knock their face together and send down a second shower into the face of the moist sweet earth . she be look radiantly happy , for it be as thrill as a lover 's hot kiss to have fix on paper something that have look beautiful to we . 
 " be you go to some one ? " ask the woman suddenly . 
 " go to some one ? " repeat Undine inquiringly . 
 " yes . I beg your pardon , " say the woman , seem terribly abash and speak more nervously than usual . " I hope you will forgive I . but I mean you look so happy and I I think you must be go to some one . " 
 " no , I have no one to go to , " say Undine . " be you go to friend ? " 
 " yes , " say the woman . 

 Undine lean back wearily on her pillow . so it be only she who be utterly alone ; even this queer grey woman have friend . 
 " where be the friend you be go to ? " she ask presently . 
 the woman wait for a long time , then she say , suddenly , " I have one ; I be go to he . " and then , after a short pause , " he be dead . " and a smile as sad as the last red light that burn on the high crag of a mountain pass over the worn face and the great grey eye . 
 Undine ask no more question . some great sorrow have shake her reason , she think . 
 the next day the woman sit at her interminable sewing and , Undine , who lay reading feel as a generous child do who be eat something sweet and can not understand that it could be less sweet to another . " would you like I to read aloud to you a little ? you must grow so tired of sit here always and sewing , " she say . 
 " thank you , " say the woman in a tone that be as far away as the look in her eye . " long ago I use to like book ; they say it be that make I so stupid . " 
 " how could that be ? " ask Undine , rest her cheek on her hand and look at she . 

 " I do not   know , but I never could learn , and I use to sit in the window in the moonlight read the book I like ; and they say it be that make 

 I so stupid ; but I do not   think it be ; I would have be stupid anyhow . " 

 then she remember the work which have drop from her hand while she speak and she stitch on fast than ever . 
 " read make no one stupid . they must be strange to say so , " say Undine . 

 " I do not   know . you see , I could only remember poem and tale , I could not   do sum or remember the table ; I be very stupid , but I understand some of 
 they 
 ; Shelley be the name of one man I use to like , but I do not understand he ; I only feel sorry for he . it be wicked , I know , but I use to wish I could have see he . I use to like he . " she speak this in the low tone peculiar to she , and more as though she be speak to herself than to anyone else . 

 " I do not   think he be wicked , " say Undine . " it be so long ago , perhaps I have forget . " 
 " I do not   know , but I think he and his wife go away from each other , and I think he love another woman ; but I forget . " 
 " he do love another woman , but I do not   think that that be any reason for not like he . it be always right to love , love as much as we can , and as long as we can , and as strong as we can , " say Undine , emphatically , raise herself on her elbow and watch the busy finger as they move to and fro . 

 the exertion tire she , so presently she lie down again , forget all about the book , and be follow her roving fancy , when the woman lay her hand softly on her arm . 
 " do you really believe it ? " she say . " say it again . " 
 " say what ? " ask Undine , look into the grey eye which for the first time be really look at she . 
 " that it be not wrong , " she whisper . 
 " not wrong to do what ? not wrong to love ? how can it be ? it be not wrong to feel warm or to feel strong , and we can as little help love as feel either . " 
 " but if it hurt other people , " say the woman slowly . 
 " then it must be silent as the dead be , who they say live , yet we never hear they . " 
 the woman sit with her hand fold in her lap . undine lie and watch she wonderingly . 
 suddenly , with the abruptness which be at all time common to she , she draw from her bosom an old gold locket that be tie to a black - velvet string , and put in into Undine 's hand . 
 " look at it , " she say . " I never feel so before but I would like to tell you . I never feel so before but I would like to tell . " 

 like to tell ! yes , we all like it . it be not only the purple dove in the deep shade of the bush , it be 

 not only the poet in his rhapsody , talk to stone and tree , but the coldest hard sinner among we who pass through life without give a sign . we all like to tell , but , alas ! too often find no comprehender , and walk through life dumb and mute with our burden . 

 Undine open the old gold locket . in it there be the face of a young girl , a pretty , weak , sensitive face , with a setting of abundant brown curl and great , timid , fawn - like eye . 
 Opposite be the face of a man a dark , handsome , sensual face with bold black eye . 
 Undine lie look at the picture , while the woman talk on in a low dreamy voice , so softly that a time she could hardly hear she . 

 " I be always stupid , " she say . " I think that must have be the reason why no one ever love I . they send I to school when I be quite a little child to see if it would do I any good , but I use to get so frightened I could never remember when we have to come up and say our lesson , and so I always stay in the class with the little girl . I think they use to like I , the very little one ; I could dress their doll and even help they with their lesson a little . you see , I be not stupid to they , but to the big girl , and they could not bear I , but they use to let I darn their stocking for they and , when any of they get into a scrape , then they use to come to I and say , " do not 

 say it be not you if the teacher ask , because you be sure not to get a prize anyhow . " and I use to say yes , because I think it would make they love I ; but it never do , it only make the teacher hate I . one of they I think like I , she always talk so softly to I ; but one day when I be shut up all alone in the dark room that open out of the schoolroom , I hear some of the teacher talk . I think they have forget I and I hear they say I be the stupid girl in the school and that they could not think how she could like I . " I do not like she , " she say , " I feel sorry for she , she be such a poor thing ; but there be not a girl in the school I care less about . " then I lie down and cry . I have be so happy when I think she love I , and when I come out the girl all laugh at I because I have be cry , and say I be afraid of the dark ; and I be not afraid at all , I like it , but I do so want some one to help I , some one big and cleverer than I be . 

 " afterwards , when I grow a great girl , I leave off try to make people love I , because it be no use . 

 " I use to get away from the other whenever I have time and sit and read all by myself . I have not many book , only some book of poetry and a tale call 
 the wide wide world 
 , and some other little book that I forget , but I read they over and over till I could repeat they by heart . I do not   know how 

 it be I could remember such thing and not my lesson . I know I try to learn they , but somehow I never could . 

 " when I be grow and wear long dress my mother die , and my father a little time after , so I have to go away from school , and I have nothing and no one to go to except one aunt . she have a beautiful little house close to the sea , with a balcony and a flower garden in front , with little white gravelled path , and she and her three little child live there alone . I think I would be so happy there and make her love I , and I think I would not read my book any more , because they say it be that make I so stupid that no one could like I . 

 " when I come there she give I a pretty little green - and - white room all to myself , and she tell I I should only have to teach the eld two child and help she a little with her needlework ; but I would make she love I if I work very hard and try to do everything I could for she . so I use to get up very early and help the nurse to dress the child and the cook to get the breakfast , and I use to work all day and late in the evening . when the child be in bed I use to get out the needlework ; and when she use to ask I if I be not tired yet , I use to say no , though sometimes I be so tired when I go up to my room I use just to lie across the foot of my bed and cry for tiredness till I go to sleep . I know it be very 

 wicked of I , but somehow it seem as though she would like I well if I say I be never tired . after a little time she send the nurse away and I have to go and sleep with the child and look after they all day and take they for walk , and she never ask I if I be tired any more , however late I sit work . you see it be all my own fault . she believe what I tell she , but it seem so hard that she should not care about I a little bit . if she have sometimes look at I as she look at the child , I do not   think I should ever have feel tired . 

 " at last one day she tell I she be expect visitor ; a friend of hers and her husband and child be come to board with we for six month , because she be very delicate and want to be near the sea . 

 " I be half sorry and half glad when I hear it . it would give I more work , but then I always fancy , before I see people , that perhaps they would like I and not find I so dull as all the other have . by and by they come . she be a pretty woman and use to sit in the parlour all day , make wax flower and basket . my aunt use to sit and talk with she , but she never take any notice of I , even when I put fresh flower on her table or bring she pretty seaweed for her basket ; and her husband I be very frightened of . I could not bear he . he use to sit in an armchair on the balcony just before the schoolroom window all day , and I 

 use to feel as if I could not teach the child anything , especially when he look in . I be so afraid of he , I wonder how anyone could love he , till one day when I see he sit there with his little girl on his knee . her head be on his shoulder and both his arm be about she , and he look down at she with such a look in his face , and he be so strong , that I run away to my room that the child might not see I . for I could not help cry ; I wish so I be that little girl . 

 " after that , early in the morning , when I use to walk on the beach with the child and his little girl , he would often meet we when he be come back from his bath and stand and talk to his little girl and sometimes to I . I wonder he do not mind be see talk to I by the other gentleman who go past we , because I always have my aunt 's baby and look like a nurse girl . I think it be very kind of he , but I do not like he and I be afraid of he . I go round another way when I see he come . he always talk so kindly to I . he say my arm be not strong enough to carry such a big baby , and he ask I if I be not tired . no one else ever do . 
 " one day he have bring a beautiful painting of a woman and hang it up in the parlour . I be pass the door with a cup of arrowroot for the baby , when he call I to come in and look at it . it be a very pretty picture . 

 " " do you know why I buy it?í he say . " because it be like you.í 
 " I could not think how anyone could think such a beautiful face be like mine , so I look at the picture again . then I feel he take my hand softly in both his , and when I look up into his face it seem to have just the look that have be there when he look at his little girl . 

 " I pull my hand out of his and run away to the child 's room and kneel down by my bed and cry , I be so happy . I never think anyone would look at I like that , and all the day I be so glad ; I never feel tired or miserable . in the evening two or three gentleman come to play whist with he , and my aunt tell I to make some eggflip for they . he have show I how to make they before and I could make they very nicely , but this evening he come into the dining - room just as I have finish , because he say he be afraid I would not do it right . we be all alone , and as he go out of the room he put his arm so softly round I and kiss my mouth . it seem as if there be a great river run past my ear , and I sit down and put my head on the table . I do not think there be any wrong in it ; I do not think at all . it be all so strange , and I be so happy . I do not think that day or for many day after . I have no time to think . you see , I be work , work all the time with the child or at housework , from early 

 in the morning when all the other people be in bed till late in the evening , and at night I be so tired I could not undress . I go to sleep in my clothe . I only know that I be happy . they say when people be idle and have nothing to do they sin , but I think people do more sin when they have no time to think , because you can love without time , you see . one Sunday evening I have time to think . they have all go to church and the little one I be take care of be asleep , and I could sit at the foot of the bed and think . I see that his love for I be not like his love for his little girl , else why do he never kiss I when even the child be by ? there must be something wrong in it . so I think I would ask he to go away very soon . I do not love he ; I hardly know if I like he , except just when I be talk to he ; but I know it would be very hard to lose he . you see , nothing else have ever love I like that . 


 " just as I be think so , I see he stand in the door . he have go with the other to church ; I do not   know how it be he come back . he come into the room and stoop down over I and ask I what I be think of . then I tell he , and he say I be a foolish little girl and tell I there be nothing wrong in his love I ; he say some kind of love between man and woman be wrong , of course , but he only love I as if I be his little girl . I be his little sunshine , he say , and 

 he do not show his love to I before other because his wife be so queer ; she do not like he to have a friend , even a man , though she do not care for he at all , he say . he have never have anyone to love he , and he long so to have some one who care for he utterly ; he ask I if I would not . then I feel as if I have be quite wrong to think it be not right to love he , and when he ask I to kiss he I do , though I never have before . then I love he well , and I feel quite glad and happy till the next day . I be dust the parlour , and I hear his wife talk to he in the other room . 

 " " I be not a fool , or quite blind either , í she say . " I understand your small game by this time . I know very well why you buy that picture , and the meaning of your pleasant look . oh , yes , I be not such a fool as you take I for , nor she , either , with her flower and her seaweed and her pretty innocent little face.í 

 " I go out of the room then , because I do not want to hear more ; but suddenly , I do not   know why , the thought come to I that they be talk about I . I ask he that evening , and he say : " you must not mind she ; she would be jealous of your aunt if you be not here . it be only her nature.í I feel very unhappy after that whenever I have time to think and be alone , but when I be near he I be quite happy , and I get to love his little 

 child so . I have it near I all day long , but I could not bear to see he play with it .
