I like so to go and put his room neat ; it be so nice to touch the brush he use every morning and to fold up his clothe and put they away , and it be so nice to touch his great - coat when I pass through the hall . one day I pick up a torn likeness of his on the floor , and I put it in my mother 's locket by mine , and that be nice , too . 


 " one afternoon , when all the other be out on the beach and I be leave at home to get tea ready , he come in . I be kneel on the pantry dresser , fill a glass pot with jam , when I look round and see he stand behind I . he come up and lift I down in his arm and carry I into the dining - room . then he sit down with I in the great armchair and hold I very close to he , and ask I if I love he , utterly , well than anything else in the world . when I say yes , he put his face down close to mine and say very softly . " then you must come away with I , far away , to another land where you and I can be alone with each other till we die , and we will make each other happy , 

 so happy.í he tell I he love nothing in the world but I ; and when I look up at he it seem as though his eyelid be wet . I lay quite still for a minute and then I try to jump up and run away , but he do not let I go . 

 " " how can you leave your wife and your little child?í I ask he , and then I creep close to he again and tell he that I love he . I do not   know what else I say ; I do not   think I even know then . 
 " but after that day I love he with another kind of love , not like the love I love he with before ; and I could not bear to be in the same room with he when there be other people , because it seem as though they must see in my face how much I love he . and every day he beg I to go away with he , but I always say , " no , no , no.í it would have be wrong of I to go , but I do not care about that , I be so wicked ; I could not bear that he should be selfish and leave his wife and his little child . if he have ask I to do anything I would have do it , I would not have care ; but I do not like he to be wicked . 

 " so many week go on and sometimes I use to get miserable and ask he to go away . then he use to hold I in his arm and kiss I , and I forget everything . you see , I be work , work all the day and at night I be tired , so tired . sometimes when I be with the child on the 

 beach in the morning I be so sleepy that I go to sleep sit on the sand . 

 " at last one day they all go away to see a great show in the next town . they go for two or three day , and I be leave to take care of the house . it seem so dreadful to have to think of be there alone for two whole day and never see he once . I cry , and in the afternoon I fall asleep on the sofa wrap in his great - coat , and do not wake till next morning . then I put the house in order and get a great heap of his stocking to darn . when I go to bed that night I be not very tired . 
 " I lay thinking and thinking , and I can not tell how it be , I seem to see so suddenly all at once how wicked I have be , and how wicked I have make he . it be just like be in hell to think of it all . I feel as if I should go mad , and at last I get up and light the candle and sit down and write to he . I do not   know just what I write , but I know that I tell he I have be very wicked ; it have be all one great lie ; I have try to look and act as though I do not care for he , and I have make he do wrong . I tell he I would never speak to he again or touch his hand , and that I would go away , but I would always love he . I must have say something more , for I write many sheet , but I do not   know what it be . perhaps it be the same thing over and over . 

 " it seem to I as though the morning would never come and I would go mad before it come . he have call I his little angel and his sunshine and I have be like a devil to he , make he sin , and now it be do and could never be undo . 

 " the next day they come . I think he have get tired of I , for when he come into the dining - room where I be stand he hardly say good - day to I or look at I . he take the letter from my hand and we never be together again . I tell my aunt that evening that I be go away . she be very angry and say I be mad and very ungrateful , but that she would be glad when I be go . then I go into the nursery and write to the teacher of the school I have be to , and ask she if she would let I come and teach the little one . I would not want money if only she would let I come at once . when I have do I sit think and it seem to I as though I must go and tell his wife everything ; it be sin , nothing else matter , and it seem as though if we tell everything that it would be less . so I get up , but when I get to the door of her room I think how angry he would be and so I go back . by and by , I go again ; but now the light be out , and when I stand close by the door I could hear her breathing and his . I listen for a little time and then I go back again to my room . the next morning when I look out at the window I see he walk on the road that lead to the beach , 

 and I never see he any more . I get an answer from my old teacher and I start that day , but I do not stay with her long . perhaps I be very foolish , but it seem to I as though , if I work very hard all my life for other people and at work I do not like , it might make it right for he a little bit . I be very foolish , but I could not help think it would be of use , a little use . I always hat so to see blood and people that be in pain ; so I get they to let I help in a great hospital , and I learn to be a nurse . I use to feel faint at first , and as though I want to run away , when I see anything dreadful , but I use to think it be help , and then I feel strong . I never hear of he any more , I think he be tired of I before I go away , and that he would soon forget I . I think so for twelve year and I never hear his name . but the other night I be sit up with another old nurse . she be tell about a gentleman with whom she have go out to South Africa . I be stir the gruel before the fire and I do not listen to what she say till I hear a name ; it be his name . then I ask she to tell I all she could about he . she tell I that he have some disease and the doctor say he must take a long voyage ; but it do he no good . at last when they get to a little town in Africa they see that he be die . he do not like his wife to come near he or do anything for he , and all the day and all the night he lie groan . 

 at last one night just before the light come they see that he be go . he lie quite still , but at last he open his eye and look all round the room . 

 " come to I , come to I , " he say . 
 " they ask he if he want his wife , but he say , " no , no ; my darling , my little sunshine , once , just once , darling.í he do not say anything more . and so now I be go to he , " say the grey woman , very quietly . 
 when Undine turn to put the locket in her hand , tear be in her own eye ; but on the woman 's face be only that strange smile , sad than any tear . 
 the voyage be almost end . that night they would be in Table Bay .

 ! what be gold ? " so we ask scornfully in the day of our ignorance . " gold ! what be gold ? " we ask it derisively . 

 King Gold sit on his throne and laugh secure , for well he know that soon or later , if he withhold his cold light , the proud knee will bend and the stubborn hand will rise and the old prayer of humanity will come from the derisive lip : 
 " oh , Gold , thou art King and Lord ; if not the God , yet a God forever , in whose hand lie health oftentime , and joy oftentime , and the desire of the heart and of the eye . pour down upon we the light of thy countenance we beseech thee , o Lord ! " 
 but the God of Gold be grow old and deaf now , like the other god , and he often let our prayer rise and die unanswered . 
 " Gold ! what be gold ? "

 to rush the world over seek for happiness be a fool 's work . be it also a fool 's to look for a life 

 which , however hard and rough , shall be high and noble , a life worth live ? 

 from be the useless plaything of a man , from dress and eating and lounge on sofas , to nurse another woman 's child , to make another woman 's bed ! will life 's change be always so , shall we never get any high ? oh , the thing of life be very little , and the soul be great . 

 she walk on till , just as the sun set , she reach the little kloof and , force her way through the rock and tree , come to the bed of the mountain torrent . she clamber down its steep bank and leap on to the smooth white sand that line its bottom . then she pause to take breath and lean against one of the great dark boulder that lie about on every hand . long year ago the rush torrent have tear they down from their home on the mountain - side , but they lie very quiet and unmovable now on their bed of white sand . over one of they , a little high up in the bed of the torrent , a tiny stream of water trickle . the drop as they fall down slowly on the face of the flat stone below have the soft silver sound of far - away evening bell , and everything else be very silent . the silver band of water as it creep through the sand make no sound , and the long low tremulous bank of maiden - hair fern , though it heave and sway to and fro in the stillness , make no sound . high on the western bank of the stream against the white dreamy evening sky ,

 EVERY 
 grace must come to an end , so philosophise the hungry child ; and even the dominion of a Mrs. Snappercaps have a limit and a termination . she and her little soul and her little torture may shut out all the great varied world for a little time ; she may seem to engulf everything for a little time , till all above , around , below be Mrs. Snappercaps and her baby ; but land must be gain at last , if it be only the land of death . 


 for Mr. Snappercaps that land might be the only one in which his poor good old soul should find refuge ; but Undine 's deliverance come near at hand when the white tent of Du Toit 's Pan 
 1 
 come in sight , gather like a flock of white bird round their monster sandheap . 


 the next evening , free and emancipate , she stand before a store in New Rush , where Mr. Snappercaps have just unload his wire and bucket . she feel very strong and very free as she stand there , with her box at her side and two shilling in her pocket , and 

 1 
 Du Toit 's Pan now a suburb of Kimberley . 


 watch the wagon roll slowly up the street and out of sight . 

 it be glorious to be alone again . alone , though the street be so thronged with the stream crowd of nigger and digger return home from the work that they kick up the red sand into a lurid cloud over their head stark - naked savage from the interior , with their bent spindle leg and their big - jaw foreheadless monkey - face , who , though they be go home to fire and meal , could hardly get out of their habitual crawl colonial nigger half dress , not half civilized , and with some hundred per cent more of evil in their black countenance than in those of their wilder brother great muscular fellow , almost tall and strong than their master , the white digger , who form a thin sprinkling in the crowd and who , in spite of the thick dust that envelop they , might be distinguish by their more quick and energetic movement .

 he be a gentleman who make his live principally at night , but he find it useful to have some ostensible employment which might serve to account for his gold chain and black cloth , if ever he find himself in the close hand of the law .

 " a gentleman throw it away one day . it have a wither rose on it then ; but I put a white bottle over it , and I hold it in the sun all day , and now it be grow , you see . " she touch its little leaf softly and caressingly with her finger as she speak . 
 " do not   you get very tired of sit still with it all day ? " ask Undine . 
 a very black look come over the child 's face as she answer shortly , " I can not   walk ; my back 's hurt . " 
 " and so you sit here alone all day nurse your flower . " 

 " mostly , but sometimes the woman who stop with father do not   always go out . I wish she always do . when mother be here she always stay in , but she be dead , " say the child . there be infinite satisfaction in the tone in which the last three word be utter . 
 " have you be long unable to walk ? " say Undine , lay her hand softly on the red head . 
 " since she beat I the night before she die . " she speak more sullenly than ever and twitch her little brown toe backwards and forwards . 
 " what do you do to try and get well ? " 
 " nothing , " say the child . " one of those gentleman that go about with the little black bag and the sugar pill , he stop and talk to I one day and he give I something to rub with , but I can not   rub it and there be no one can . " 
 " can not   I rub it for you ? " 
 the child look up half suspiciously , then her eye brighten a little . 
 " it be in the tent , and Mary Jones would be angry if anyone go in when she be go out . do you live far from here ? " 
 " I do not   live anywhere , " say Undine . " I be look for work . " 
 the child scrutinize she from head to foot , with the shrewd suspicious old woman 's look that the face of field child so soon learn to wear . then she say : 

 " what kind of work ? " 
 " anything ironing . " she would have add , " needlework , " but a short experience have make she very wise , and she know that a man 's dog be an animal more enviable than a woman 's friend if so be the one be mistress and the other maid . needlework must be do for woman , ironing might be for man , so she decide in favour of the ironing . 
 her red - headed little companion meditate for a time , then she say , " Mary Jones have lot of iron in the tent , and she always drink too much to do it . if you stay till she come I think she will let you get some . 
 so Undine sit down on the ground beside she and wait . 



 XVII . 
 LITTLE iron 

 six 
 month after , Undine stand in her own little tent , sort and pile into heap the ironing she have just finish . 

 ' twas a New Rush winter 's morning ; in the blue sky there be not a cloud , and if it be cold and numb in the inside of tent and on the shady side of gravel - heap , out in the sunshine it be warm and genial . 

 she be hurry to get out into it , and truly to impartial eye there be nothing very alluring in the interior of the little tent . ' twas a small place , six foot by eight , and hold three packing - case . the large be a table , cover over with shirt . the second be a bed ; it have low side which lie flat on the ground and serve to keep off the wind which at night blow in chill under the skirting . the small have a kind of tick ; it be a desk and general repository . it do not lock , but that matter less , as its only content be paper scribble over and clothe that would not have pay a Kaffir the time it take to steal they . it be an empty place , and cheerless it would have look to other eye ; but to 

 Undine not a yellow water stain in the canvas nor a mark in the cracked pole , nor a knot in the rough case but have its own story , and a pleasant familiar face show itself in each of they . even the old black bottle stand in the corner make home , more home . she might have change it now for a candlestick , but so many pleasant thought hang round its old black neck that the bottle keep its ground . 

 place on a tray one of the pile of iron , and put on the huge white kappie which have replace the battered silk hat and very much add to the respectability of the iron woman , she go out into the sunshine , button down the door after she . 

 the tent stand in a quiet corner of the Camp on the outskirt of the North End . the only very near neighbour be a family of dutch Boers who camp on the right . on all other side it be surround by low gravel - heap , 
 1 
 among which the tent nestle like a white bird in a yellow nest , as Undine say when describe it to her little break - back friend . 

 she go to visit she this morning before take her work to its destination , and find she bask in the warmth at the back of the tent , a veritable diogene , with only her head and shoulder stick out of the great tub in which she have ensconce herself .

 Dťbris . 


 in answer to her visitor 's look of inquiry , she say , " the ground 's so wet I can not   lie on it , and in here it be so nice . I can rock from side to side . just see ! " and she put the tub in motion , lean heavily first on one elbow and then on the other . 
 " and the rose ? " 
 " oh , it be all right , but it seem as though spring would never come , " say the girl , touch with her thick little forefinger the still leafless and brown slip that stand in the side of the old three - legged pot . 
 " you only stay such a little while yesterday , you must not go soon today , " she say ; and Undine put down her tray and sit down on the ground beside she . 
 " I can not stay very long today , " she say . " I must try and find the owner of those shirt . three month ago they be bring I , and no one have ever call for they ; I be afraid the person to whom they belong must be poor and need they , they be so fine and so old and worn . " 
 " he be wait so long , he will not   mind wait a little long , " say the girl , rest her head in her companion 's lap and look up into her face with her clear grey eye . 
 " tell I what you write about last night , " she say . 

 Undine 's hand rest on the same great shock of wild red hair , and the broad freckle face that look up at hers be the same that six month 

 before she have see for the first time ; yet it resemble that face only as a face awake resemble the same face asleep . it be like a dark room into which the sunshine have look . 

 " I do not write anything , " say Undine , as she pass her finger tenderly along the line in the low forehead ; " I be so tired I go to sleep with the pen in my hand , and when I wake the candle have quite burn out . " 
 " and have you not anything to tell I ? " 
 " no . I have be so busy all the morning . " 
 " and can not   you think while you work ? " 
 " sometimes , not often ; but yesterday evening , when I be put the collar into starch , a little story come to I that seem beautiful then , though it do not now . shall I tell it to you ? " 
 the child nod ; and Undine , run her finger through and through her coarse hair , begin : 
 " a mother be lie on her bed , dying , and at her side be a very little baby . the people who stand round her thought she know nothing , see nothing ; and truly she see none of they . she feel only the touch of the little baby 's finger upon her breast , but she see what no one else could see in the far end of the room be two , draw ball from a box which have no bottom ; and Death 's ball be the pure white and Life 's be the blood red . 

 " death be very tall and calm and his face be smooth and white , like a face cut out of marble ; his 

 eyelid be half closed and in the eye beneath they lie the shadow of wonderful dream . round he be a mantle of many cold grey tint , and his wing be fold close against his side . 

 " a ball be draw , and it be Death 's white ball ; so the mother know that she must go to he ; but when they be go to draw again , she pray and say : 
 " " stay ! stay ! o death ; give Life my child!í for she fear he , he be so still and cold , and they be strange wonderful dream that wander beneath his eyelid . 
 " and Life say , " let the mother see what we have to give it , and she shall decide who be to have the child.í 
 " and Death bow his head slowly . 

 " now Life be very beautiful ; her hair be like the yellow glory of the sunset , and her limb be strong and soft and round , and her breast be as white as an open lily . her cheek be red , so red that the tear trace could hardly be see on they , and her white dazzle wing be always quiver and expand , yet they never raise she or take she from the earth . she be very lovely , and the bright robe she wear be of spotless tender green , the colour of the first shoot on the white - thorn tree ; only here and there , where it turn up a little , the lining show it be red and have clot on as though it have be dip in blood . she be very beautiful ; but 

 when the mother look at her forehead , knit with thought and pain , and at her large wide - open eye through which the light and darkness chase each other endlessly , she fear she also . 

 " life speak first , and her voice be like the singing of the bird in spring - time , and the murmuring of the crowd in a great city , and the weeping of a lonely woman at a graveside , all strangely blend . 
 " " look in my eye , í she say , " and see what I have to giveí ; and the mother look . 
 " in the street of a great city roll the carriage of a rich man , and the mud from its wheel spring up into the face of two who be poor and hungry and stand at the corner of the street talk . 
 " " whose carriage be that?í ask the one . 
 " " the man who rid in it be the rich and most fortunate man in all this city , í answer the other . " from his boyhood upwards all that his hand have touch have turn to gold . Misfortune have never cross he . his very dog live long than another be and die easy death . we be friend once in our youth , but now he count his gold by million , and I have nothing but a starve wife.í 
 " " and why do you not go to he for help?í 
 " " because how should he pity I who have never know want , and how should he remember I who have entertain lord and princes?í but still when they part the poor man turn his step towards the house of the great . 

 " " if I have but half that one of his horse eat I would be happy , í he think . 
 " the fortunate man be walk in his garden . he be very fat , and the only walk he ever take be up and down its gravel path . the air be rich with the scent of the flower , and the light of the afternoon sun make the drop of the leap fountain sparkle more brightly than the diamond on his finger . a small bird be bath itself in the water . 
 " " now , í say the rich man , " if it be not too much trouble , and the shot worth more than the fruit it eat , I would kill that bird.í 
 " then he think of the grand dinner he be to give the next day , and how his beautiful daughter be to marry one of the great lord who would be there . 
 " then he think how they all envy he his grand old mansion and his priceless horse ; then he look up and see the poor man stand between he and the sun . he do not know he , for it be very hard to remember people who be so shabby , and so he ask he who he be . the poor man tell his story , and when he have finish go back out of that beautiful garden sorry that he have enter it . 

 " then the rich man walk up and down again and bask in the sunshine . it be a man 's own fault if he have trouble and be poor and friendless , 

 for the world be a good world . there be no help for he but in the grave , the poor man have say , and the fortunate man think , as he walk up and down , what a very great fool he must be . it be such a nice pleasant world this , with its great red sun warm one on a chilly afternoon all for nothing , and ripen one 's fruit and vegetable and ask for no pay . it be such a nice pleasant world this , with such a nice pleasant sea , over which pleasant ship could bring pleasant wine and turtle from other pleasant land . he moisten his lip when he think of his old , old wine ; and then he think of another disagreeable dark place that the man have speak of , where there be great cobwebs which be not round old bottle and live thing that be not gay horse . that be the place he do not like to think of ; it make the sweat stand in great drop on his red neck . life have be so good to he ; she have give he all the sweet and keep back all the bitter ; she have bring no tear to his eye since he have be old enough to tell a sixpence from a penny ; it would be hard to leave she now , when all man envy he . so he pull out his watch with its setting of jewel and wonder when the dinner hour would come , and try to forget that other hour . and at last the dinner hour come , with its guest and its laughter and its wine . and at last that other hour come also the only hour of which we be all sure ; and the 

 fortunate man , who have never suffer and never weep and never pity , go to the place he fear where the live thing and cobwebs be . nobody miss he , nobody want he back again not his pretty daughter , for she have all his money . 

 " now , when the mother see all this , she would have give the child to Death , for she say , " it be as well he have die a baby.í 
 " but Life prevent she : " I have other thing to give , í she say . 
 " and the mother look . it be a garden again , a wild neglect garden where the flower and creeper grow rank and free in each other 's arm , and beauty be not measure out . at the root of a great tree , almost enfold and hide by the shrub that grow around it , stand a man . his face be young and one to be pity by the old and wise , for it be very glad and full of hope . in his arm , press close to he , be a woman , and not one of the flower have a face so fair as her ; but , deep in her eye , creep a look like the look which creep in the eye of the serpent in that First Garden long ago . they be sweet long kiss ; and the word she speak to he be sweet , the sweet old word of love and faith which woman speak to man ; and he believe she . 

 " his heart grow very strong and great through the mighty love that come to he , and their life path lie before he in a mist of light and beauty . truly 

 God 's world be good , and the life he give great and beautiful , and only the pure and true of heart be worthy of it . so he think ; and look in the eye of the woman he love , and press his lip to her , and draw she close to he , for he never see the serpent 's look that glide in they . 

 " but the day come , at last , when he do see it when she look into his face and laugh , and he know that when he press the woman he love to his heart it be only the grey old father of lie he have hold . now , life be for he that woman and that woman be evil , he become evil too . for the sake of what he have once love , he deceive all woman , and drank and curse , and gain gold by evil , and spend it in sin ; and man say that , wherever he pass , you might trace he by the ruin and evil he leave behind . yet they envy he , for the woman love he , and where other man would have starve he make gold . he might eat of the fruit of the earth and satisfy himself : its gold , its wine , or its woman they be all free to he who have no conscience to restrain and no faith in a high power . 
 " the woman he have once love be tell of he how the devil befriend his own , how he sin and come to no evil , and enjoy life as other man could not .

 " there be a street with great and noble house , and out at the door of one of they come a young man . his shoulder be bent and , as he walk , his eye be fix upon the ground ; only once he look up at the great house at his side and see the face of two soft woman look out of a large window . then he clench the finger of the hand that hang at his side till the nail go into the flesh , and clench his tooth and swear under his breath a bitter oath . 
 " ' twas a strange presumptuous oath for a man to swear who wear brown threadbare clothe out at elbow and boot that be split and who live in a garret ; for he swear that the day should come when those rich man should ask he to their table and he would refuse to come , when those white proud woman whom he curse in his bitterness should covet a smile or a word from he , when the world should know he and call he great . this he swear and go home to his garret . 

 " it be a dreary empty place where the sunlight never enter and where dry bread be eat and 

 where nothing pleasant ever come except only a young girl with hard work - wear hand . she be the landlord 's daughter , and she creep in every day to rub the dust off the rotten table and turn the straw mattress and carry out the ash , if there be any . in the long evening , when to save light he would sit there think in the dark , she would sit there too , close beside he with her hard little hand in his , just as she have do when he come there three year before . she have be a child then ; she be a woman now ; but it make no difference to she . 

 " one evening she do not come , and he sit there alone , think , think . the room be very quiet , but there be a great war rag in the man 's heart . at last he bring his hand down on the table and swear between his clenched tooth , as he have swear that day before the rich man 's house . 
 " " she will not help I in my work , í he say ; " she and her child will be a weight on I , drag I down . if I stay here it will conquer I . I must leave she , I must leave she , for she can not help me.í 
 " so in the grey dawn of the winter morning he stand in the door of his room , ready to leave it for the last time . she be labour up the stair with a great heap of coal in her arm .

 " year come , year go ; his hair grow whiter ; his shoulder stoop lower yet ; and alone and in bitterness he labour on .

 " and at last it come . the world call he great ; it write of he in its paper ; man talk of he on the street , and woman in their house . the child learn to lisp his name ; rich man ask he to their dinner ; noblewomen come to visit he , only that they might say that they have see he . 

 " he be very great , and his fame be very great ,

 " the other clerk call he fool ; if they have know how his night be spend they would have call he so more often . when their day 's work be over they go out to amuse themselves , but he only shut himself up in his room and walk up and down and pray and write himself half mad before the morning come .

 " so he think then , for he be weary , and throw himself down on his bed . perhaps he sleep , but his eye be heavy and red the next morning as he stand behind the counter , sell ribbon and print . 

 " so this poor clerk go on , month after month , pray and write all night and measure off dress by the yard all day ; but at last it happen that one of his dream take a human shape , and a pair of clear still eye look into his life and make he rich than the great prince of the Golden Isles , whose house and whose shoe be cover with jewel . it be true , as man speak , that the eye belong not to he but to a woman who be nothing to he a woman who be high above he and who would surely be carry , some day , to another man 's home . yet when he be beside she she speak to he kindly , and in her face he find the beauty in her mind , the truth he dream of . he know that she be his though she do not love he , for he love she , and no one could ever take she from he , not she herself . 
 " he hear at last that she be go to be marry , and then he leave the town and go far , far away , and for a little time there be a heavy aching at his heart all day as he stand behind the counter or sit alone in his silent room . but at last the ache go , and there be only gladness leave . he have not her body , it be true , but her beautiful soul be live somewhere and it be true and real , and the earth be never again quite empty for he . 

 " the year pass on , and they still call he a fool , for he make no money . he never stay long enough in any place , but wander on from town 

 to town and land to land , just when the longing seize he . sometimes a child 's face , or a reach of sea beach , or the charm of snow - crown mountain make he pause a little , but have get all they have to give , he wander on again . 

 " he make no money and no friend , this poor fool of a clerk . only sometimes , when pain or sorrow would draw people to he , they would enter his life for a little time ; but when they be comfort they would go out of it again , and he would go on with his wandering and sing his song and smile and love the beautiful green old earth . 
 " sometimes his song be sad , but oftener they be glad , for it do not take much to make he happy a little stream of sunlight break in through the good within the window , or the shadow which the tree cast as he pass below they on his way to work or to lie on the grass on Sunday morning and watch the rippling in the pool of water ; that be enough to make life sweet to he so sweet that , when the death he have once long for come to he , he be almost sorry to leave it . yet it seem so pleasant to think of lie deep in the soft old earth he love , and he be glad he have live . there be not one night of sleepless agony , nor one hour of bitterness he would have miss , even if he might . it be all good , look at from the end . life lie very beautiful behind , and death be not terrible , only very strange . 

 " he die young and they bury he in the earth he love ; but there be not a tear shed over he . for why ? what have he do all his life ? sell a few yard of print and ribbon , cast up a few account , suffer a little agony , pray a little , doubt a little , comfort a few people who be sad ; and for the rest live much as the bird live , sing and love and revel in the sunshine . 
 " " I have that to give , í say Life .

 the owner of the shirt , she have be tell by the Kaffir who bring they , live near the Circus ; that his name be W. Brown the shirt themselves tell she ; but to discover his whereabouts seem a hopeless task . 
 Most people answer she shortly enough . one old woman , in answer to her question , begin the long story of one Bill Brown , who might be the Bill Brown she be in search of , who have live at Graaff Rienet , who have set out for the Fields , but who , as turn out in the sequel , have die before reach they .

 little iron and a digger

 " meet again ! meet again ! " poor human heart that must still their ache with such vain word . meet again ! who ever meet again ? the child we love go from we and come back to we a man , and all other praise the change ; but we , even while we run our finger through his curl , we hunger for the little child that sit upon our knee . 
 we part with the friend of our childhood , and we say , " we part only for today ; through life we shall often meet again , " and it may be we clasp hand often in the year that come and talk of the old day ; but we know , though we never say it , that the two who part have never meet again , that the sea of time have run up between we , and we can not touch . who can part , forever ; only when we come so close that nothing separate we can we meet again , only when what bind we be not my need of you or your need of I nor any chance circumstance , but a deep ingrain likeness of nature that can not pass away .

 it might have end in she not go to the ball that night , but at that moment the child pass they with the bright flower in its hand . 
 " what a lovely flower ! " say the mother , and she hold out her hand for it ; but the child clasp it tightly in his fist and hold it close against his little breast . 
 it be only a moment 's work for the gentleman to unclasp the little finger and put the flower into the mother 's hand . the child do not cry ; he only press his little thin arched lip together and droop the lid over the blue eye with which he look at they . he be only a baby : there be no sin in take it . " you see the very god have condescend to interfere in my behalf , " whisper the gentleman . " this rise mean that you be to go and wear it here tonight . " 

 he lie it very softly on her breast and whisper word , so softly that only the ear in which they be speak could catch they ; and when the mother rise 

 to go into the house she say , " well just for one hour , just for one , you know . " 

 and so she go to the ball that night and dance , the lovely of all the woman there , with that bright flower at her heart ; and all praise she and look at she . 
 and that night , alone , when the nigger who have be leave to watch he have go out to spend the five shilling , Albert Blair die . 



 XIX . 
 ALBERT BLAIR 


 " Vat jou go en trek , Ferreira ,

 Swaar dra , swaar dra ... "

 whistle the swell nigger next morning as he walk , switch his cane , in the direction of Undine 's tent . 

 generally she rise early , but this morning she be sleep late and so heavily that he have to knock two or three time at the tent pole before she come to unbutton the sail . 
 " do you want any needlework ? " ask the nigger , touch his hat quite respectfully , for , even with a salary of six pound a month , five shilling be not to be despise . 
 Undine say she want no work . 

 the nigger look disappointed . he have hop she would take the work , and show as great an

 objection to accept payment for black skirt as for iron shirt . 

 " you see , my master die last night , and Mrs. Blair want she mourning quickly . do not   you think , if I be to bring some stuff now , you would be able to do it for she ? " 
 there be no doubt today about the iron - woman 's daftness . she take no notice of his question , but say , after a pause , " what do your master die of ? " 
 " well , you see , " reply the nigger , rest his hand on the head of his cane and lean elegantly forward , " I do not   just rightly know . he come here just to have a look at everything , and he take ill , something wrong inside , and the doctor they will not   let he travel ; and this six month he be be lie here , and they have   be say he be go to die , but he never do till last night . " 
 have get so far , the nigger turn round and look across the road to see what it might be the iron - woman see that make her eye look so strange . he could see nothing but just a blade or two of grass which have not yet be tread down and which be heavy with the morning dew ; so he look at she again . 
 " when be they go to bury he ? " 
 " tomorrow morning . they have   put he in a house in the yard ; for Mrs. Blair she be frightened of ghost . " 

 there be nothing to be gain by waste more word over she just now , so the nigger resume his " Swaar dra , swaar dra , " and , without touch his hat , turn away and walk jauntily whistle down the road . 
 Undine stand in the doorway and look after he . there be sparrow hop about at the tent - side , pick up crumb and insect ; and digger pass with their sleeve roll up above their elbow , walk briskly , whistle , some of they , for the morning air be fresh and make they feel that life , though it might mean small find and hard work , be a pleasant thing and worth the having . some of her child die every day , and nature might go about forever in deep weed and mourn if she take the trouble to lament for they ; so she go on smile , though the well love and the dear have just go smile , smile , when our heart be break . why should the sky be cloud and the bird fly home hungry , because in one small tent a man lie stiff and white ? man whom woman 's heart have yearn over die just so every week , and the world rock on the same . 

 Undine sleep heavily all day , a heavy sleep but trouble by many dream ; and when she wake the sun have long set . she go out to the barrel that stand at the back of the tent , and drain the last drop of water into the mug . she be thirsty , parch with thirst , but she feel no hunger . the slice of 

 bread , very dry now , still lie upon the box unfinishe . 

 she sit down on the side of her bed and hold her head between her hand and try to think , but her brain seem very numb . after about an hour she stand up and go out , take the road by which she have come yesterday evening . it be very dark , but she know her way well . 
 the Compound be very quiet tonight . there be no one on the veranda , no light in the house . only in the little tent at the back there be a light visible , and presently two man come out . the night be still and , though they speak low , she could hear every word that pass : 
 " put the candle and match down , Jack , just there inside the door and button it down tight , " say the first man . " I wonder they like leave it alone like this without a soul in the place . dog might get in . " 
 " no fear of that while this dog lie here , " say the second . " if I be not with you , I expect you would rather be pretty near anywhere than here ; he would think no more of tear you than of growl , if you try to go in there alone ; he do not   half like it as it be , for all that I have   have the feeding of the beggar for the last six month . down , Prince , down ! " 
 the man pass close to where Undine stand . 
 " I tell you what , Jack , " say the first , " that coffin be damn heavy . my shoulder ache . " 

 " charge it all in the bill , " say the second with a laugh : 

 " ten little nigger boy 
 fiddle over wine ; 
 one get so jolly drunk , 
 and then there be nine , nine , nine . " 

 then they go out at the gate , and the Compound be silent once more . 
 by and by Undine go round and open the gate and walk in . 
 " Prince , Prince , old boy , " she call softly ; for Prince have rise to his foot and utter a low growl at the sound of approach footstep . " Prince , have you quite forget I ? " 
 the dog do not leave his post , but when she come close to he he lay his head against her knee . 
 " Prince , Prince ! oh , Prince ! " 

 he seem to understand she , for he utter a long low growl , and they crouch down together at the entrance . be 
 he 
 listen for the sound of his master 's breathing in the quiet tent ? or be it only 
 one 
 who remember how they two wait and listen , long ago ? 

 only the heavy breathing of the dog and the quick low breath of the woman break the stillness and be hear loud and clear in the quiet night ; but in the tent , in the tent , there be deadly stillness . 

 it be near midnight now , and in the street passenger - cart rumble past , bear home Toit 's Pan 

 visitor from the fast - close house of amusement . 

 now she stand up and loosen the low button that fasten down the canvas door . stoop low , she go in , and the dog follow she , lie down close to the doorway and utter a low short howl . then it be quite silent in the tent , and very dark . feel her way along its side , her finger touch at last the cold back of a chair , but that be not what she look for ; then the edge of a small table ; then something low than the table , long and narrow but with nothing inside . she feel that it be empty , so she move on softly . her hand be on the iron bedpost , then on the smooth sheet , and then on something cold O , God how cold ! 
 she take the sheet down off his face , and the cheek of the live woman be press close to the cold face of the dead man . in his ear she whisper the wild word of love that to the living she would never utter wild passionate word , the outpouring of a life 's crush - out love , the breaking forth of a fiercely suppress passion . and the dead man lie so still ; he do not send she from he ; he do not silence she ; he understand she now ; he love she now . she will see his face once more before it go , and then she will creep close to he , and lie there , and never leave he . 

 in its place near the door she find the glass candlestick and match , and when she have strike a light she come and stand with it in her hand at the 

 bed 's foot till her eye have grow accustomed to it ; then she look up . 

 it be a calm white face that lie there above the sternly fold arm a calm white face with the old smile , half scornful , half defiant , on the delicate arched lip . 
 the old face ! what use to cry aloud to it ! mad , mad , and fool ! be there room in those sternly fold arm for she ! he have live alone and self - sufficient ; he have die alone . there be no room for she now . 
 with a cry , as of one whose last hope have pass away , she let the light fall upon the floor , and the glass break into a thousand fragment . but she stay at the bed 's foot till the grey light glimmer through the canvas . then she creep out and leave he . 
 a few hour afterwards , when all New Rush be astir again , the young wife come in to see her husband for the last time . she have never look so lovely as that day in her flow crape , with the great tear of fear in her baby eye when they tell she to stoop down and kiss he . 
 " I can not , I can not , " she cry ; " I be so afraid . " and as she turn to go out , the trail crape roll the broken glass upon the floor . 
 that be all that tell of last night 's watch . 



 XX . 
 alone with the star 

 water 
 ! Water ! 

 she have sleep again all day , and now that she awake it be dark , and she be parch with thirst and there be no water none in the barrel , none in the jug ; her tongue clave to the roof of her mouth and her vein seem scorch by liquid fire . she shake the barrel fiercely in her anger and try to draw the tap out with her tooth . there must be some water in it , if only one could get it ; it seem to she some cruel living thing withhold life from she ; and when she find she could do nothing she run round and round the tent in the vain hope of grow cool . in her delirium it seem that behind she a whole host of small hideous being follow , howl old woman with long canine tooth that touch their breast , old man with hunchback and little twinkle eye which they close tight and then open suddenly : before , behind , they follow she ; at every side they press she ; and her thirst grow great , till her tongue refuse to move and keep they off by word . 

 " Water , water , water ! " be all she could murmur . and at last , as if in answer to her cry , water come . the great cloud that have make the night so dark burst , and the great torrent pour down on the earth . in an instant the heavy canvas sail be drench , and she kneel down eagerly , hold they in both hand and suck they . then she lie down and let the rain fall on she till the fever leave she and a great shivering seize she . 
 she go into her tent and climb into the box , but her hand seem powerless to undo her wet clothe , so she draw the blanket over she and lie there till morning . 
 " Mother , " say the child of the Dutchwoman opposite " mother , perhaps some wicked man have be to kill the Englishwoman in the little tent . three day the sail be hang loose , but we never see she come out or do iron . we think she must be dead . " 
 " nonsense ! " say the mother . " do not   you have anything to do with she ; she be a bad woman . " 
 " how do you know that ? " ask her husband , who sit at the door , smoke his pipe . 
 " because I ask she the other day if the man who live with she be her husband , and she say no . and I ask she if he be any relation of her , and she say no . so she must be bad , " say the wife . 

 nevertheless , when her work be do , curiosity 

 lead the dame over to the Englishwoman 's tent . she look in at the door and at first thought there be nothing but the three packing - case in the tent ; then , in the farth of these , which lie bottom downward , she notice the purple blanket move , and go up to it . 

 " you be very sick , " say the Dutchwoman in English , well than boer generally speak . 
 Undine open her eye , but do not answer . 
 " you be very sick , " repeat the Dutchwoman . " what be your name ? " 
 " Undine , Undine Bock , " say Undine , slowly , as though puzzle to remember what it really be , and go back to the old name of her childhood . 
 " great heaven ! " say the Dutchwoman . " do you remember I Sannie Muller ? " 
 " yes , " say Undine ; but her eye have close again . 
 " can I do anything for you ? " Sannie ask with some real kindness in her voice , as the memory come to she of the little schoolmate who , in company with her monkey , have be first and foremost in all evil and forever in disgrace . 
 " no , thank you , " say Undine . 
 but the woman remain sit by she till it grow dark ; then she light a candle and stand at her side , say as she do so : " I will come again during the night and see you . " 

 " Mother , " ask the little child who have be 

 wait for she in the road , as she trot along at her side , " be the Englishwoman very sick ? " 

 " yes , " say the mother . " she will be dead in the morning . " 
 the Dutchwoman have work hard all day , and when once she fall asleep she do not awake . 
 but the little tent have another visitor that night . 
 not long after the Dutchwoman leave , a great , rough curly head push itself in at the door , sniff for a moment , and then four black paw carry it up to the side of the box . Undine be rouse by a soft warm touch on her hand and when she open her eye the rough old face be close above her , look down at she . her mind be too confused and dull for his presence there to cause she even the vague wonder . she only move her finger feebly and call his name , " Prince , Prince . " 
 he step over the low side of the packing - case and lie down across her foot , with his head turn to one side so that he could watch she as he lie there . 
 a very quiet sleep follow , and Undine do not know when the candle drop into the bottle , or when Prince move high up so that his head rest on her breast . she know nothing till she wake at one o'clock . then she raise herself a little on her elbow , look round , and fall back heavily again on her pillow . 

 the rack pain , the fever , the dull confusion 

 of brain , all have vanish . free from pain , calm and clear as she have never feel before , she lie there , yet cold , strangely cold . what do it mean , this strange feeling ? she lie wonder , think , with her hand fold on the dog 's black head . then the truth come to she suddenly . 

 death only that , nothing more . what she have long and pray for ; what she have look for in the muddy pool ; what she have sigh for in day of emptiness it have come at last . 
 again she raise herself and again fall back heavily upon the pillow . " not death , not death ! " she say , " not death ! anything else death be too horrible and I , I be so young , so young to die ! " 

 what be the use of cry out ! she only grow stiff and cold and her breath come slow and heavy in the closed tent . she would leave it and go out into the starlight , she would be braver there . the great horror that be upon she give her strength , and she push the dog from she and creep slowly over the side of the low box . there she lie long , and then again , inch by inch , crawl on hand and knee , she reach the doorway . the skirting that cross it , three inch high , be hard to pass , and again she lie still ; but when she turn her head and catch sight of clear starlight outside , she creep on once more . still on her hand and knee , and fall sometimes with her face into the 

 dust , she gain at last one of the low gravel - heap 
 1 
 and lie down on its side . 

 she look up at the old star that she have look up to and love from her childhood as other man love their friend of flesh and blood the dear old star that have shed their light on the thatched roof and stone wall of the old farm on the Karoo ; that have look in at the window of the little whitewashed room and on the leaf of the small brown Testament and the little child who cry and pray there ; the same and yet , tonight , look so strange and new to she . over the tumult and agony that reign within , they speak a great peace , and she lie still and watch they . 
 ' twas one of the gorgeous night when the sky , shoot light from a million point , overwhelm and silence we ; and the little circle of our life , that have seem to fill all creation , sink to its proper size a shadow , a breath of wind that , be or not be , matter not . 
 high over her head be one great blue star that give a steady and unflickering light . at this she look with dark wide - open eye till it seem to speak to she as clearly as the priest speak who stand at the bedside of the dying with bread and wine , reproof and blessing , whereby he hop to help the soul in its last struggle among the water . 

 " be death so horrible and ghastly to you ? " say 

 1 
 Dťbris . 


 the star , " so ghastly that even the pain and suffering and despair that be in life grow beautiful in your eye ? I be only your brother , " say the star , " a few million year old than you , and I know nothing ; but I have see some thing a few . I have see the sun pour forth his light and heat as a great heart pour its life - blood for other . I have see it fall on a world dead and silent , and awake it ; till in place of death there be life , and for silence sound and ceaseless change . I have see a world find birth through that light , even those strange and tiny creature 
 1 
 who deep at the floor of the sea have form their graf and a new land ; the wave have roll back from it and the land that be build from their skeleton have become tree and grass and a million form of life ; on these other creature have live ; and these again have die that other might have life ; and at last man have come , to bring one of whom from the shapeless germ in which he lie plant innumerable die , and his very next of kin be sacrifie that he may grow and be . I have look long and carefully , " say the star , " and I have see that the thing which you call death be the father of all life and beauty . till life go , till blood flow , no high life can come . there be nothing add to nature , nothing take from she . she have only so much in her hand , and with that she must do all thing . would she build well , she must pull down 

 1 
 Coral . 


 first ; would she raise a new world , an old must sink ; would she double a flower , the seed of the single must go ; and to make a man a million million form have be and be not . 

 " without death there be no change , without change no life ; without the shedding of blood no good thing . 
 " if what you fear in the death that be upon you be not change but a fearful endless silence and annihilation , then take comfort , " say the star ; " I have be young and now be old ; I have see great ebb and great flow , and myriad never - end change ; but such death as you dream of I have nowhere see . nature be too poor to lose , too poor to let rest ; her work be not yet do ; she have other thing to make . 
 " Mark you well , I know nothing , " say the star ; " and what you be , or I be , or the gravel be on which you lie , I can not tell , and what we mean I can not tell ; only that which I have see I speak of . 
 " the stump now burn at your side , it be a great brown lifeless stump an hour or two ago , now a lurid glow mass shoot out flame and heat , crack and change every moment . it will be a small heap of ash soon , but the light and heat be in it before the match touch it , and I know they be not lose , only do other work in other form . 

 " I have be young and now be old , " say the 

 star ; " yet if I should say I have see death as you fear it , I should lie . Change I have see and desolation , but no death . take comfort . " 

 and she be comfort and look upwards with her arm fold and almost a smile on her lip . 
 for , as in our hour of sin and weakness , we weep because the great ever - change , many - wave current on which we find ourselves will flow on just the same when our small wave have spend itself , so , in our moment of sight and strength , a joy , calm and mighty , come to we when we see that the great current will flow on uninjured , unchanged by our loss , in its deathless progress . 
 she lie still and be comfort . and what if the star never speak , and only her own thought be throw back to she ! if it be to a bedside with priest , wafer , and book , or to a gravel - heap under the star , that peace and strength come , be they not the child of the soul , and no outcome of wafer , priest , or star ? though bless be all three if they can call they forth in the hour of that battle the last and strong . 
 she rest till it seem as though a mist be creep over the brilliant night sky , and then as though the smoke from the fire pass before her eye . she raise her hand slowly as though to wave it from she ; but it grow dark , and one by one the star vanish . then she know that it be the shadow of death that lie between she and they . 

 slowly she turn away her head , and even in that darkness could see lie between the two great stone the stump , now coal from end to end with blood - red crack upon its surface . 
 the cold be grow great , so she creep a little nearer the coal and lie with her face to it . 
 be it because the glow light , see through the mist , bring back a night of long ago , that she hear in the dim delicious confusion the voice that have call she so tenderly under the red lamplight in the little hall ? 
 " my little girl , my own little girl Undine , " it say over and over , and the soft tear of gladness fill her eye , and in delicious dreamy darkness it seem as though his arm be close around she . 
 presently the moon rise and look over the ridge of the tent into the little yard among the gravel - heap . the glow stump have burn out and go to ash between the great round stone . 
 before they , in her little purple print , with her foot cross and her head rest on one arm , lie Undine . 
 her white kappie lie near she and cast a grotesque shadow , like a man 's face with long nose and chin ; and the light glisten on her soft brown hair . 
 there be nothing else to be see in the little yard .
